**Summary.** This paper introduces Exploratory Digital Alchemy (EDA), an advanced simulation technique that enhances existing inverse design methods by incorporating Metadynamics principles. EDA allows researchers to explore the full range of potential self-assembled structures in colloidal systems without needing to know the target crystal structure beforehand. By applying this to LJGP and OPP potentials, the authors successfully map out complex free energy landscapes, revealing multiple stable and metastable phases.

**Why it may be interesting.** The methodology of enhancing statistical sampling techniques (MetaD) for materials design is highly relevant. It provides a computational framework applicable to complex many-body systems where the energy landscape is unknown or multi-modal, bridging simulation theory with physical discovery.

<details markdown="1"><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** The primary goal is to develop an enhanced forward design scheme to discover novel, stable self-assembled colloidal structures by overcoming the limitation of existing inverse design methods.

**Main result.** The proposed Exploratory Digital Alchemy (EDA) successfully explores broad potential energy landscapes, identifying multiple coexisting and metastable crystal phases for given particle interaction potentials.

**Method.** EDA enhances Digital Alchemy (DA) by integrating a Metadynamics-like bias potential into the generalized ensemble framework, allowing unbiased exploration of the design space.

**Model / system.** The study models colloidal particles interacting via specific pair potentials: a 2D Lennard-Jones Gauss Potential (LJGP) and a 3D Oscillating Pair Potential (OPP). The analysis focuses on mapping the Free Energy Surface (FES) as a function of potential parameters.

**Key observables.** Free Energy Landscape ($\Phi$), crystal structures identified via Minkowski Structure Metric (MSM), and stability ranges for different phases (e.g., square vs. hexagonal lattices).

**Important parameters / regimes.** Alchemical parameters ($\alpha$, such as $r_0$ or $\phi$), temperature ($k_B T$), and the bias potential parameters used in Metadynamics.

**Assumptions / limitations.** The approach assumes that combining DA with MetaD's self-exploration mechanics can effectively map complex, multi-modal free energy landscapes without needing a predefined target structure.

**Figures summary.** Figures illustrate the conceptual shift from constrained DA to exploratory EDA (Fig. 1), show potential energy profiles correlating stability with parameters (Fig. 2 for LJGP), and display FES maps revealing multiple stable/metastable phases across varying potentials (Fig. 3, Fig. 5).

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the limitations of DA, proposes EDA as an enhancement using Metadynamics bias accumulation, details its application to both LJGP (2D) and OPP (3D) systems, presents results showing phase identification across parameter space, and concludes by validating the method's ability to map metastability.

</details>

<details markdown="1"><summary>Abstract</summary>

Digital Alchemy (DA), introduced by Van Anders et al., is a statistical mechanics-based generalized thermodynamic ensemble method that employs computer simulations to optimize colloidal particle design. This approach applies the principles of statistical mechanics to predict and tailor particle attributes that lead to desired self-assembled structures or material properties. However, as an inverse design method, its main limitation is that the target structure must be known \textit{a priori}. Therefore, the optimal design from DA does not guarantee the targeted structure is the most or the only stable one. This highlights the importance of forward design with an exploratory scheme for optimizing novel colloid designs, which becomes more suitable in such cases. In this paper, we introduce Exploratory Digital Alchemy (EDA), an enhanced forward design scheme that begins by releasing the constraint of the target crystal from DA, followed by an exploration-oriented bias that has been extensively used in enhanced sampling methods such as metadynamics (MetaD). We demonstrate the utility of EDA through examples involving particles interacting via a two-dimensional Lennard-Jones Gauss potential (LJGP) and a three-dimensional oscillating pair potential (OPP). We applied EDA to study the free energy landscapes given different potential parameters of LJGP at different temperatures. With the exploratory scheme, we've also successfully identified a wide range of OPP potential parameters that stabilize metastable Frank-Kasper phases. Our approach fuses the standard DA framework with metadynamics, which could potentially be useful for studying alchemical reactions in a generalized ensemble.

</details>

<sub>[↑ back to top](#top)</sub>

<a id="paper-2606.13388"></a>
### [From 2D Yang-Mills to Calogero-Sutherland via a colored particle](http://arxiv.org/abs/2606.13388v1)

**Authors:** Marcia Tenser, Amilcar R. Queiroz  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** other · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2606.13388v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks
**Topic relevance:** `analog quantum simulation` **1/5**

<div class="figure-strip-hint">↔ Scroll figures horizontally</div>
<div class="paper-figures-scroll">
<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2606.13388_figures/2606.13388_fig1.jpg" alt="Figure 1">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 1.</b> Figure 3: Potential V (Y ) for G = SU(2) and K = 1. Other values for K simply shift the curves vertically.</figcaption>
</figure>
<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2606.13388_figures/2606.13388_fig2.jpg" alt="Figure 2">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 2.</b> Figure 4: G = SU(3): (a) the 2D lattice from TSU(3)/S3. The fundamental unit cell is 2-simplex, a triangle. The honeycomb lattice is obtained after acting upon its vertices with permutation matrices. Blue and green shifts correspond to a P1 and a P2 action, respectively. The entire plane is covered by copies of this hexagon structure, generated by large gauge transformations. In (b) the potential V (Y 1, Y 2) assuming Kˆı = 1, ˆı = 1, 2, 3.</figcaption>
</figure>
</div>

**Summary.** This paper analyzes the quantum mechanics of Yang-Mills theory coupled to a charged particle on a cylinder. By rigorously applying gauge constraints and transforming the Hamiltonian, the authors demonstrate that the resulting system maps precisely onto the Calogero-Sutherland model for SU(N). This establishes a profound link between non-Abelian gauge theories and exactly solvable integrable quantum systems.

**Why it may be interesting.** The deep connection established between a fundamental gauge theory (Yang-Mills) and an exactly solvable quantum integrable model (Calogero-Sutherland) provides powerful mathematical tools for understanding complex many-body dynamics in theoretical physics.

<details markdown="1"><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** The study investigates Yang-Mills theory coupled to a charged particle on a cylinder, aiming to derive an effective quantum Hamiltonian.

**Main result.** The non-Abelian gauge dynamics are shown to reduce exactly to the integrable Calogero-Sutherland model for SU(N).

**Method.** The analysis involves solving Gauss' law constraints using Wilson lines and decomposing the resulting Hamiltonian into a form solvable by mapping it onto known quantum many-body systems.

**Model / system.** The system is 2D Yang-Mills theory ($G=SU(N)$) coupled to a charged particle on a cylindrical manifold. The effective dynamics are described by a Hamiltonian whose potential term matches the Calogero-Sutherland form.

**Key observables.** Energy eigenvalues, spectral flow conditions, and the structure of the pairwise interaction potential V(Y).

**Important parameters / regimes.** The gauge group rank N (e.g., SU(2), SU(3)), particle mass m, and coupling constants $g_{YM}$. The limit $r 	o \infty$ is a key regime analyzed.

**Assumptions / limitations.** The method assumes solving the Gauss law constraint explicitly prior to quantization, and relies on decomposing fields using the Cartan-Weyl basis.

**Figures summary.** Figures illustrate the physical setup (particle on a cylinder), the lattice structure for SU(3) related to the Weyl group, and the explicit form of the potential V(Y).

**Paper structure.** The paper proceeds by setting up the classical dynamics via Wong's equations, imposing gauge constraints (Gauss law), quantizing the system using Wilson lines, transforming to the Cartan basis, and finally demonstrating the Hamiltonian's equivalence to the Calogero-Sutherland model while proving its Weyl invariance.

</details>

<details markdown="1"><summary>Abstract</summary>

We study Yang-Mills theory coupled to a particle on a cylinder, where gauge invariance and compactness reduce the dynamics to a finite dimensional quantum system. In the Abelian case, this yields a model equivalent to the Landau problem on a torus, with a degenerate ground state structure. We generalize this construction to non-Abelian gauge groups and show that, for SU(N), the system reduces to a one dimensional quantum many body problem with a singular Calogero-Sutherland-type interaction.

</details>

### [Quantum Network Routing based on Surface Code Error Correction](http://arxiv.org/abs/2606.12781v1)

**Authors:** Tianjie Hu, Jindi Wu, Qun Li  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** quantum information and computing · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2606.12781v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks
**Topic relevance:** `entanglement & information structure` **1/5**

<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2606.12781_figures/2606.12781_fig5.jpg" alt="Figure 5">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 5.</b> Fig. 5. Example decoding graph of the SurfNet Decoder. Each vertex is a measurement qubit and each edge is a data qubit. For illustration, the growth speeds on Erasures, Core, Support are {1/2, 1/8, 1/4}. (a) Initial State. Red vertices denote Syndromes, Purple lines denote Erasures, and Solid Grey lines denote the Core part. (b) Growth Step 1. Green lines denote newly added edges for each cluster. Even clusters are marked in Yellow. (c) Growth Step 5. Blue lines denote newly added edges for each cluster, and Green lines denote existing edges. After this step, all clusters become even and finish growing. (d) Estimated Error Pattern, where Black lines denote data qubits with errors.</figcaption>
</figure>
</div>

**Summary.** This paper introduces SurfNet, a novel quantum network architecture designed to overcome noise limitations by combining two parallel communication channels. It encodes data using surface codes and splits the information into a robust 'Core' part (sent via entanglement) and a bulk 'Support' part (sent physically). The authors develop advanced decoding algorithms and an optimization framework to maximize throughput while maintaining high fidelity.

**Why it may be interesting.** The integration of fault-tolerance concepts like surface codes directly into network routing protocols provides a concrete framework for realizing large-scale quantum communication infrastructure, which is highly relevant to open quantum systems research.

<details markdown="1"><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Designing quantum network protocols that maintain high reliability and efficiency despite unavoidable channel noises and erasure errors.

**Main result.** The proposed SurfNet architecture, utilizing a dual-channel transfer mechanism with surface codes, significantly enhances communication fidelity compared to existing methods.

**Method.** The authors combine resource optimization via Integer Programming (IP) formulation for routing with advanced error correction techniques like the novel SurfNet Decoder.

**Model / system.** The system is a quantum network modeled on a lattice structure where data qubits are encoded using surface codes. Information transfer is split into a 'Core part' (transferred via entanglement) and a 'Support part' (transmitted physically as photons).

**Key observables.** Communication Fidelity ($ho$), Network Throughput, Pauli Error Thresholds.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Fiber fidelity ($\gamma_i$), Noise thresholds ($W_c, W$), Facility capacity ($\eta_r, \eta_e$).

**Assumptions / limitations.** The analysis assumes perfect measurements for simplicity in some parts; the IP formulation is noted as an approximation requiring relaxation to LP.

**Figures summary.** Figures illustrate the SurfNet architecture (combining entanglement and plain channels), examples of surface code structures, error correction processes using syndrome patterns, and comparative performance plots showing fidelity vs. throughput across different network scenarios.

**Paper structure.** The paper progresses from defining the core problem (noise mitigation) to proposing SurfNet's dual-channel design. It details the use of surface codes for encoding, introduces the Core/Support split, develops novel decoding algorithms (SurfNet Decoder), and finally frames the entire routing challenge as a resource optimization problem solvable via IP formulation.

</details>

<details markdown="1"><summary>Abstract</summary>

Quantum networks encounter unavoidable channel noises and erasure errors, presenting a huge obstacle in designing protocols that attain both high reliability and efficiency. Typically, quantum networks fall into two categories: those utilize quantum entanglements for quantum teleportation, and those directly transfer the actual quantum messages. In this paper, we present SurfNet, a quantum network that inherits the main advantages from both categories. It employs surface codes as logical qubits for encoding messages, and utilizes two parallel communication channels to fault-tolerantly transfer each surface code in a modular manner. Our approach of using surface codes can timely correct both operational and photon loss errors within the network, and the integration of the two channels within the network can greatly improve network throughput. For the implementation of SurfNet, we propose a novel network architecture, designed to better integrate surface codes into quantum networks. We also propose a novel error correction decoder, designed to fully utilize the modular characteristic of surface codes within our network. Simulation results demonstrate that SurfNet with its decoder significantly enhances the communication fidelity within quantum networks.

</details>

<a id="paper-2606.12806"></a>
### [Quantum Reservoir Computing for Short-Term Power Load Forecasting in Resource-Constrained Energy Systems](http://arxiv.org/abs/2606.12806v1)

**Authors:** Mansi Od, Param Pathak, Nouhaila Innan, Muhammad Shafique  
**Type:** both · **Category:** disordered systems and neural networks · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2606.12806v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks
**Topic relevance:** `methods for driven-dissipative` **1/5**

<div class="figure-strip-hint">↔ Scroll figures horizontally</div>
<div class="paper-figures-scroll">
<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2606.12806_figures/2606.12806_fig1.jpg" alt="Figure 1">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 1.</b> Fig. 1: Conceptual overview of the proposed hardware-efficient QRC forecasting framework. Energy load data is encoded into a fixed quantum reservoir, transformed into reservoir features, and mapped to load forecasts through a quantized classical readout. The framework is evaluated under exact simulation, finite-shot sampling, and realistic IBM backend-noise models.</figcaption>
</figure>
<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2606.12806_figures/2606.12806_fig2.jpg" alt="Figure 2">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 2.</b> Fig. 2: Overview of the proposed QRC forecasting framework. The pipeline constructs T = 24 input windows, extracts 5N observables per time step from a fixed quantum reservoir, compresses the temporal states into 245 aggregated features, and trains an Elastic Net readout for load prediction. After training, the readout is quantized to {8, 6, 4, 3, 2}- bit fixed-point precision and evaluated under finite-shot and hardware-noise settings. The GA search is performed offline to select N, L, encoding, and coupling strength κ for each dataset.</figcaption>
</figure>
<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2606.12806_figures/2606.12806_fig3.jpg" alt="Figure 3">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 3.</b> Fig. 3: Quantum reservoir circuit at one time step. Each of the N qubits receives the double rotation RZ(π˜x) · RY (π˜x) for feature encoding, followed by a frozen Haar random Rot(α, β, γ) gate and a brickwork entangling block whose CNOT offset alternates between even and odd pairs across layers. The encode and entangle pattern repeats L times before measurement of single qubit Pauli expectations ⟨Zi⟩, ⟨Xi⟩, ⟨Yi⟩ and nearest neighbour correlators ⟨ZiZi+1⟩, ⟨XiXi+1⟩, yielding 5N observables per step.</figcaption>
</figure>
<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2606.12806_figures/2606.12806_fig4.jpg" alt="Figure 4">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 4.</b> Fig. 4: ElasticNet readout training pipeline. Standardized reservoir features R and targets y feed a 5 fold cross validated grid search over the regularization strength α (30 log spaced values) and the mixing ratio ρ ∈{0.05, 0.1, 0.15, 0.2}, which set the ℓ1 and ℓ2 penalty weights λ1 = αρ and λ2 = α(1 −ρ). The selected combination yields a sparse weight vector ˆw whose predictions are inverse scaled to physical units.</figcaption>
</figure>
<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2606.12806_figures/2606.12806_fig5.jpg" alt="Figure 5">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 5.</b> Fig. 5: Post training quantization (PTQ) pipeline. The trained FP32 weights pass through an optimal clipping search over [0.5σ, ∥w∥∞] followed by uniform rounding to a k bit grid with step size ∆= 2c∗/(2k −1). Three rounds of iterative residual refinement then fit a Ridge correction on the prediction error and re-quantize, suppressing the systematic bias that grows at low bit widths. The procedure produces five deployable readouts at {8, 6, 4, 3, 2} bits with corresponding memory savings of {75, 81.2, 87.5, 90.6, 93.7}%.</figcaption>
</figure>
</div>

**Summary.** This work proposes using Quantum Reservoir Computing (QRC) for energy load forecasting, designed specifically for deployment on memory-limited edge devices. The key innovation is applying post-training fixed-point quantization to the classical readout weights while keeping the quantum reservoir fixed. Results demonstrate that 6-bit precision maintains high accuracy while drastically reducing memory footprint, proving a resource-aware approach for near-term quantum time-series applications.

**Why it may be interesting.** While focused on energy forecasting, the core methodology—combining quantum feature mapping (reservoir) with highly resource-constrained classical ML readout (quantized Elastic Net)—is a novel paradigm for developing hardware-efficient AI models applicable to complex physical simulations or data analysis in quantum computing.

<details markdown="1"><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** Developing accurate Short-Term Load Forecasting (STLF) models for resource-constrained edge devices while maintaining performance under limited memory, finite measurement budgets, and hardware noise.

**Main result.** The framework successfully quantizes the readout to 6-bit precision, preserving full-precision forecasting performance while achieving an 81.2% reduction in readout memory.

**Method.** A Quantum Reservoir Computing (QRC) framework is used where a fixed quantum reservoir transforms temporal inputs into high-dimensional features, and only a classical Elastic Net readout is trained and subsequently compressed via post-training fixed-point quantization.

**Model / system.** The system uses a QRC architecture with an entangled quantum reservoir state derived from time-series data. The training involves optimizing the linear readout layer using Elastic Net regularization on aggregated reservoir features, followed by aggressive low-bit quantization for deployment.

**Key observables.** Forecasting accuracy (RMSE, MAPE), Readout memory reduction percentage, and performance stability across varying bit widths ($\{8, 6, 4, 3, 2\}$).

**Important parameters / regimes.** Quantization bit width ($k$), Number of qubits ($N$), Reservoir size/feature dimension, Noise sources (finite-shot sampling, IBM FakeTorino/Marrakesh noise models).

**Assumptions / limitations.** The quantum reservoir remains fixed throughout the process; only the classical readout weights are quantized and trained. The performance degradation below 6 bits is dataset-dependent.

**Figures summary.** Figures illustrate the QRC framework pipeline, compare RMSE vs. Bit Width showing stability at 6 bits, and validate forecast predictions under both ideal simulation and realistic hardware noise conditions for two energy datasets (Tetouan and Spain).

**Paper structure.** The paper details the QRC model setup, describes the Elastic Net training process, introduces the Post-Training Quantization pipeline with residual refinement, and validates the entire framework across multiple noise regimes and bit widths.

</details>

<details markdown="1"><summary>Abstract</summary>

Short-term load forecasting is essential for reliable energy management, but practical deployment on edge devices requires models that remain accurate under limited memory, finite measurement budgets, and hardware noise. This work proposes a hardware-efficient Quantum Reservoir Computing (QRC) framework for energy load forecasting, where a fixed quantum reservoir transforms temporal input windows into high-dimensional features and only a classical Elastic Net readout is trained. To reduce deployment cost, the trained readout is compressed using post-training fixed-point quantization at bit widths from 8 to 2 bits. The framework is evaluated on the Tetouan and Spain energy load datasets under exact statevector simulation, 512-shot finite sampling, and realistic hardware-noise models from IBM FakeTorino and IBM FakeMarrakesh. Results show that 6-bit readout precision preserves full-precision forecasting performance while reducing readout memory by 81.2%. Below this point, degradation becomes dataset dependent, with Tetouan showing stronger sensitivity and Spain degrading more gradually. Hardware-noise validation further shows that the trained readout transfers to noisy reservoir states without retraining. These findings support quantized QRC as a resource-aware forecasting approach for near-term quantum time-series applications.

</details>

**Summary.** The paper introduces an LLM-driven agentic framework designed to autonomously design complex quantum circuits for tasks like QML and VQE. By integrating web search, expert critique, code generation, and validation in a closed loop, the system demonstrates superior performance compared to manual or task-specific methods. This establishes AI as a viable paradigm for automated scientific discovery in quantum computing.

**Why it may be interesting.** This work directly addresses the bottleneck of human expertise in designing optimal quantum circuits by proposing a general-purpose AI paradigm that can automate scientific optimization workflows across different physical domains.

<details markdown="1"><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** The design of high-performing quantum circuits, required for tasks like QML feature mapping or VQE ansatz generation, currently relies heavily on specialized human expertise.

**Main result.** An autonomous agentic framework utilizing LLMs was demonstrated to iteratively and systematically design quantum circuits that achieve state-of-the-art performance compared to existing methods.

**Method.** The system employs a closed-loop workflow involving seven components (Exploration, Generation, Discussion, Validation, Evaluation, Storage, Review) powered by LLMs for iterative refinement of circuit designs.

**Model / system.** The work focuses on designing quantum circuits (ansätze or feature maps) parameterized by angles ($	heta$) to prepare quantum states $|\psi(	heta)angle$ used in variational algorithms like VQE. The underlying physics involves molecular Hamiltonians and qubit representations.

**Key observables.** Image classification accuracy (for QML); Ground state energy estimation error relative to chemical accuracy thresholds (for VQE).

**Important parameters / regimes.** Qubit count ($N$), number of trainable parameters ($	ext{n\_params}$), CNOT counts, and circuit depth/complexity.

**Assumptions / limitations.** The framework assumes LLMs can effectively manage complex scientific reasoning across multiple iterative steps; specific technical limitations include restricting methods like ADAPT-VQE due to complexity constraints.

**Figures summary.** Figures illustrate the seven-component agentic workflow, performance comparisons (e.g., feature map vs. RBF kernel), and scaling analysis of circuit parameters/errors versus qubit count or module inclusion.

**Paper structure.** The paper details the architecture of the autonomous agentic system, applying it first to QML feature maps and then expanding its scope to generate complex, physically motivated ansätze for VQE in quantum chemistry.

</details>

<details markdown="1"><summary>Abstract</summary>

The design of high performing quantum circuits remains largely dependent on human expertise. We introduce an autonomous agentic framework that employs large language models (LLMs) to conduct iterative quantum circuit designs under explicit design constraints. Our system integrates seven components: Exploration, Generation, Discussion, Validation, Storage, Evaluation, and Review. These components form a closed-loop workflow that combines web-based knowledge acquisition, literature-grounded critique, executable code generation, and experimental feedback. We evaluate the framework on two tasks: quantum feature map construction for quantum machine learning and ansatz generation for variational quantum eigensolver applications in quantum chemistry. In image classification benchmarks, the best generated feature map outperforms representative quantum feature maps and, when scaled to larger qubit counts, surpasses the classical radial basis function kernel. In molecular ground state estimation across seven molecules, the generated ansatz attains competitive accuracy with widely used chemically inspired and hardware-efficient constructions while satisfying the imposed scaling constraints. These results establish LLM driven agentic system as a viable paradigm for automated quantum circuit design and illustrate how AI systems can participate in iterative scientific optimization workflows across scientific domains.

</details>

<a id="paper-2606.12724"></a>
### [Block algebra for morphing circuits](http://arxiv.org/abs/2606.12724v1)

**Authors:** Rui Chao  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** quantum information and computing · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2606.12724v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks

<div class="figure-strip-hint">↔ Scroll figures horizontally</div>
<div class="paper-figures-scroll">
<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2606.12724_figures/2606.12724_fig1.jpg" alt="Figure 1">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 1.</b> FIG. 1. A morphing circuit with J = 2 contraction rounds; reproduced from Ref. [ST25,</figcaption>
</figure>
<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2606.12724_figures/2606.12724_fig2.jpg" alt="Figure 2">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 2.</b> Fig. 1]. The mid-cycle code C with [[N, K, D]] sits at the center; the two end-cycle codes</figcaption>

<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2606.12724_figures/2606.12724_fig3.jpg" alt="Figure 3">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 3.</b> FIG. 2. Surface code: site layout (left) with translation vectors x, y, and parity-check</figcaption>

<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2606.12724_figures/2606.12724_fig4.jpg" alt="Figure 4">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 4.</b> Fig. 3a shows the hex-grid surface-code circuit of Ref. [MBG23], and Fig. 3b shows Con-</figcaption>
</figure>
<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2606.12724_figures/2606.12724_fig5.jpg" alt="Figure 5">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 5.</b> FIG. 4. 6.6.6 color code: site layout (left) with translation vectors x, y, and parity-check</figcaption>
</figure>
</div>

**Summary.** This paper develops a block algebra formalism to describe morphing circuits used in quantum error correction. It presents four explicit constructions that encode established codes like the surface and color codes into this general algebraic structure. This advances the theoretical understanding of fault-tolerant computation by providing systematic circuit design tools.

**Why it may be interesting.** This work provides a powerful, systematic algebraic toolset for designing fault-tolerant quantum computation protocols by relaxing hardware connectivity requirements in QEC circuits.

<details markdown="1"><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** The research focuses on developing an algebraic framework, using block algebra notation, to describe 'morphing circuits' for quantum error correction.

**Main result.** Four explicit constructions (I-IV) are presented for CNOT-based CSS morphing circuits, allowing known codes like the surface and color codes to be represented in this general algebraic form.

**Method.** The authors employ an algebraic viewpoint by viewing contraction schedules as Gaussian elimination patterns over block stabilizer matrices, generalizing translation-invariant code structures into polynomial sums.

**Model / system.** The model is Quantum Error Correction (QEC) using CSS codes (e.g., surface and color codes). The circuits are represented abstractly via block algebra notation involving permutation matrices acting on syndrome measurements.

**Key observables.** Mid-cycle code stabilizer matrices ($H_X, H_Z$), qubit connectivity degree, and the resulting logical error rate after simulation.

**Important parameters / regimes.** The number of contraction rounds ($J$) and the specific commutation relations between polynomial parameters (e.g., $PR = QS$).

**Assumptions / limitations.** It is assumed that known translation-invariant codes can be mapped to polynomial sums within this general block algebra framework.

**Figures summary.** Figures illustrate morphing circuits, comparing surface code derivations to the new algebraic constructions (e.g., Fig. 3), and show site layouts for various color codes.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the concept of morphing circuits algebraically, presents four specific constructions (I-IV) tailored to different known codes (surface/color), details the mathematical constraints required for each construction, and concludes with simulation setup notes.

</details>

<details markdown="1"><summary>Abstract</summary>

Morphing circuits are a new paradigm for quantum error correction that relaxes hardware requirements. We present four constructions for CNOT-based CSS morphing circuits with explicit qubit connectivity degrees. All four constructions are specified in block algebra notation, with entries in algebras generated by permutation matrices. The first three are obtained by rewriting existing surface- and color-code morphing circuits; the fourth is a new three-round construction modeled on the 6.6.6 color code. The surface-code construction recovers the morphing circuit of Ref. [ST25] for two-block group algebra codes. Numerical search then instantiates these permutation matrices using regular representations of finite groups.   [ST25] M. H. Shaw and B. M. Terhal, Phys. Rev. Lett. 134(9), 090602 (2025).

</details>

<sub>[↑ back to top](#top)</sub>

<a id="paper-2606.13118"></a>
### [Hamiltonian-Aware ADAPT Variational Quantum Eigensolver for Molecular Ground-State Simulation](http://arxiv.org/abs/2606.13118v1)

**Authors:** Runhong He, Chao Liu, Xin Hong, Qiaozhen Chai, Junyuan Zhou, Ji Guan, Guolong Cui, Shenggang Ying

**Summary.** The paper introduces Hamiltonian-Aware ADAPT-VQE, an advanced algorithm designed to improve the construction of quantum circuits for molecular ground-state energy calculations. By incorporating explicit knowledge of the underlying molecular Hamiltonian into operator selection and refining pruning techniques, it achieves superior accuracy while drastically reducing computational overhead compared to current state-of-the-art methods.

**Why it may be interesting.** This work directly addresses resource constraints (circuit depth/measurement count) in quantum chemistry simulations, providing a physically informed method to build complex ansätze necessary for simulating strongly correlated electronic systems relevant to AMO physics.

<details markdown="1"><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** The core challenge is designing compact, efficient quantum circuits (ansätze) for Variational Quantum Eigensolver (VQE) to accurately simulate the ground-state energy of practical molecules on near-term quantum hardware.

**Main result.** The proposed Hamiltonian-Aware ADAPT-VQE algorithm significantly outperforms existing methods by achieving higher accuracy with smaller ansätze and drastically reduced measurement costs for molecular systems like H2O and BeH2.

**Method.** It introduces a novel operator selection criterion that incorporates local Hamiltonian information, moving beyond simple parameter magnitude checks. It also implements a problem-adaptive pruning strategy to maintain ansatz compactness while guaranteeing convergence.

**Model / system.** The study focuses on molecular electronic structure simulation using the molecular Hamiltonian ($\hat{H}$) in second quantization form. The methods are benchmarked across small molecules (BeH2, H2O, NH3) at stretched bond lengths to induce strong electron correlation.

**Key observables.** Variational energy error (compared to FCI), ansatz size (number of operators), and measurement cost (total number of fermionic Hamiltonian terms evaluated).

**Important parameters / regimes.** Chemical precision threshold ($10^{-3}$ Hartree); the coupling strength derived from the Hamiltonian coefficients, $|h_{a_i}\sin(2	heta^*_i)|$.

**Assumptions / limitations.** The primary approximations involve using the UCCSD ansatz structure and assuming that incorporating local Hamiltonian information provides a sufficient guide for operator selection.

**Figures summary.** Figures compare energy error vs. ansatz size/measurement cost across algorithms; Figure 4 compares parameter magnitudes ($	heta^*_i$ vs. $|h_i \sin(2	heta^*_i)|$) to show the benefit of Hamiltonian awareness; Figure 5 illustrates the effectiveness of operator pruning.

**Paper structure.** The paper first establishes the limitations of existing ADAPT-VQE variants (ADAPT, Param-ADAPT) regarding locality and plateaus. It then details the HA-ADAPT-VQE algorithm, which integrates Hamiltonian information into selection and adds an adaptive pruning step. Finally, it presents systematic numerical experiments on multiple molecules comparing performance metrics.

</details>

<details markdown="1"><summary>Abstract</summary>

Designing compact ansätze in Variational Quantum Eigensolver (VQE) is crucial for solving energetic problems of practical molecules on near-term quantum devices. However, existing Adaptive Derivative-Assembled Pseudo-Trotter (ADAPT) ansätze face two challenges: improper operator selection and accumulation of degraded operators. In this paper, we propose the Hamiltonian-Aware (HA) ADAPT-VQE algorithm to address these issues. First, we establish a novel excitation operator selection criterion. It breaks the local constraint of existing criteria by incorporating Hamiltonian information, prioritizes physically meaningful excitation operators, and incurs no extra classical or quantum computational overhead. Furthermore, we develop a problem-adaptive method for discriminating and pruning redundant excitation operators stemming from improper selection and inevitable degradation. This method balances redundant operator pruning and convergence guarantee, and is applicable to ansätze with arbitrary scales. Systematic numerical experiments on typical strongly correlated molecular systems demonstrate that our HA-ADAPT-VQE avoids energy plateaus and outperforms baseline algorithms in terms of energy error, ansatz size, and measurement cost. This work offers an efficient, robust ansatz construction paradigm, facilitating the development and practical deployment of large-scale VQE in quantum chemistry.

</details>

### [Quantum Logic Codes: Complete Transversal Logical Clifford Instruction Sets for High-Rate Stabilizer Quantum Error Correcting Codes](http://arxiv.org/abs/2606.13521v1)

**Authors:** Adam Holmes

<figure class="paper-figure-card">

A small core code (left) carries a complete logical-Clifford basis ISA at low circuit depth. Two composition operations grow the code parameters while preserving that ISA: tiling (×r, top) places r copies side by side, raising the logical-qubit count to 2r at fixed distance and supplying inter-copy addressable CZ; concatenation with the Steane [[7, 1, 3]] code (×ℓ, bottom) replaces each physical qubit by an inner block, tripling the distance per level at fixed k. Combining the two yields the family [[ 7ℓr n0, 2r, 3ℓd0 ]] with logical Clifford group Sp(4r, F2) and rate...</figcaption>

<figure class="paper-figure-card">

</figure>
</div>

**Summary.** This theoretical work develops a deep understanding of how local transversal gates can generate universal logical operations on quantum error correcting codes. By constructing 'Quantum Logic Codes,' the authors demonstrate methods to achieve a complete, low-depth instruction set architecture necessary for scalable, fault-tolerant quantum computation.

**Why it may be interesting.** The rigorous mathematical framework connecting physical hardware constraints (locality $W$) to abstract computational power (full Clifford group) is highly relevant for designing practical fault-tolerant quantum computers.

<details markdown="1"><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** The study aims to characterize the structure and determine lower bounds on the circuit depth required to implement a full logical Clifford group using local transversal gates within stabilizer quantum error correcting codes.

**Main result.** The authors constructed 'Quantum Logic Codes,' a high-rate non-LDPC CSS code family possessing a constant-depth complete 2-local transversal logical Clifford basis instruction set architecture (ISA).

**Method.** The work uses symplectic geometry and algebraic constraints derived from analyzing how local physical gates act on the stabilizer group structure to establish bounds on achievable logical operations.

**Model / system.** The model is based on CSS stabilizer quantum error correcting codes, which encode physical qubits into blocks. The analysis focuses on realizing fault-tolerant logic by generating the full logical Clifford algebra using transversal gates.

**Key observables.** Circuit Depth (D), Logical Pauli Operators (S, CZ, etc.), and the structure of the reachable set within $	ext{Sp}(2K, \mathbb{F}_2)$.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Code parameters $[[n, k, d]]$, locality $W$ (1-local, 2-local), and asymptotic scaling exponents like $eta \approx 0.2823$.

**Assumptions / limitations.** The analysis heavily relies on the 'confinement hypothesis' regarding the logical action of local gates, and approximations are made when treating W-local operations as depth-one.

**Figures summary.** Figures illustrate single-layer transversal gate layers (W-local), specific constructions like the Rotated Surface Code S gate and Toric Code CZ gate, and tables detail the required depth for various logical Clifford basis generators on different code families.

**Paper structure.** The paper progresses by first establishing general lower bounds on circuit depth based on code parameters. It then analyzes the algebraic structure of 1-local and 2-local gates using symplectic forms. Finally, it presents specific constructions achieving constant or low polynomial depth for a complete logical Clifford ISA.

</details>

<details markdown="1"><summary>Abstract</summary>

We study the structure and transversal logical capabilities of stabilizer quantum error correcting codes. Among our results, we identify universal lower bounds on circuit depth to generate a full logical Clifford algebra, and develop novel constructions of logical transversal gates including a new depth-one transversal phase $\mathrm{\overline{S}}$ gate in the rotated surface code and a depth-one intra-block $\mathrm{\overline{CZ}}$ gate in the 2D-toric code that generalizes to all odd distances and all lengths $L\ge3$, respectively. Finally, we construct a high-rate non-LDPC CSS code family with parameters $[[n,\sqrt{n},Θ({n^β})]]$ where $β\approx 0.2823$ in one demonstrated case, that provably possesses a constant-depth complete 2-local transversal logical Clifford basis instruction set architecture (ISA) composed of all individually targeted $\mathrm{\overline{S}}$, $\mathrm{\overline{SHS}} = \sqrt{X}$, and $\mathrm{\overline{CZ}}$ gates. This ISA is depth-one for certain subfamilies that we design and generally constant-depth under certain conditions. The code family is built from a small code with parameters $[[n_0, 2, d_0]]$, and is tunable in the standard way: it tiles out to form utility-scale logical qubit counts, and it scales up through concatenation to achieve higher distances and error suppression. We show that this construction preserves the depth-one complete transversal logical Clifford basis ISA when composed with these commuting construction actions, inheriting structure from the core codes so that at scale the complete logical Clifford basis ISA remains depth-one up to depth-two addressable operations between tiled cores. We call these Quantum Logic Codes.

</details>

### [Quantum walk-based optimisation for capacitated vehicle routing with homogeneous and heterogeneous fleets](http://arxiv.org/abs/2606.12856v1)

**Authors:** Edric Matwiejew, Aidan Smith, Callum Neill, Paulo Santos, Ugo Varetto, Jingbo Wang

**Summary.** This paper develops and compares two quantum walk algorithms (PS-QWOA vs. I-QWOA) for solving the Capacitated Vehicle Routing Problem (CVRP). The PS-QWOA is shown to be theoretically superior because it efficiently encodes the problem's combinatorial constraints into a product space, leading to better convergence rates and lower computational overhead compared to prior methods.

**Why it may be interesting.** The work provides a concrete, structured quantum algorithm for a classically hard combinatorial problem by mapping constraints onto the structure of the quantum walk's product space, which has implications for designing resource-efficient quantum circuits.

<details markdown="1"><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** The paper addresses the challenge of optimizing the Capacitated Vehicle Routing Problem (CVRP), an NP-hard combinatorial optimization problem, using quantum computation.

**Main result.** The Product-Space Quantum Walk-Based Optimization Algorithm (PS-QWOA) consistently outperforms the Indexed QWOA (I-QWOA) across various performance metrics, showing superior probability concentration on low-cost feasible solutions.

**Method.** The authors adapt quantum walk theory by constructing a continuous-time quantum walk over a product space encoding CVRP solutions. They use variational optimization techniques to minimize an objective function related to the problem cost.

**Model / system.** The model is the PS-QWOA, which uses a Hamiltonian derived from graph structures (transposition and Hamming graphs) acting on a product Hilbert space ($\mathcal{H}_\pi \otimes \mathcal{H}_a$). The dynamics are governed by interleaved unitary operations.

**Key observables.** Feasibility Probability ($P_{	ext{feas}}$), Optimal-Feasible Amplification ($\mathcal{A}_{	ext{opt}}$), and the classical optimization cost (number of objective function evaluations).

**Important parameters / regimes.** Number of customers ($n$), number of vehicles ($K$), circuit depth ($p$), and penalty parameters ($\lambda$).

**Assumptions / limitations.** The analysis relies on exact state-vector simulation for small instances ($n \le 8$) and assumes the applicability of structured product-space walks to constrained combinatorial spaces.

**Figures summary.** Figures compare performance metrics like $\Delta P_{	ext{feas}}$ and $\Delta \log_{10} \mathcal{A}_{	ext{opt}}$ between PS-QWOA and I-QWOA, showing the advantage of PS-QWOA as problem size increases. Other figures detail graph structures and cost distributions.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the CVRP formulation, details the PS-QWOA ansatz by defining its product space structure ($	ext{G}_\pi + 	ext{G}_a$), compares it against I-QWOA using rigorous metrics ($P_{	ext{feas}}, \mathcal{A}_{	ext{opt}}$), and concludes that PS-QWOA is superior due to better scaling and lower classical overhead.

</details>

<details markdown="1"><summary>Abstract</summary>

The capacitated vehicle routing problem (CVRP) is an appealing candidate for quantum optimisation due to its combinatorial complexity and practical importance. However, the problem's constrained search space poses a challenge for such quantum algorithms. We introduce a quantum walk-based optimisation algorithm (QWOA) for the CVRP with homogeneous or heterogeneous vehicle fleets, addressing this challenge through a continuous-time quantum walk over a product space that coincides with combinatorial structures intrinsic to the CVRP solution space. Relative to the prior QWOA-based formulation, this approach reduces the per-layer gate complexity from $\mathcal{O}(n^{3}\log n)$ to $\mathcal{O}(n^{2}\log n)$ and supports a circuit parameterisation schedule generated by a fixed number of classical parameters. Exact state-vector simulation on instances with up to $n=8$ customers and $K=3$ vehicles demonstrates improved convergence to low-cost solutions using markedly fewer objective function evaluations, with the advantage broadening as problem size increases. These results identify structured product-space walks as a promising tool for optimisation over constrained combinatorial spaces.

</details>

<a id="paper-2606.13387"></a>
### [Representation-Induced Symmetry Trapping in Adaptive Variational Quantum Simulations of Multi-Reference Topologies](http://arxiv.org/abs/2606.13387v1)

**Authors:** Hermawan Kresno Dipojono  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** quantum information and computing · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2606.13387v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks

<div class="figure-strip-hint">↔ Scroll figures horizontally</div>
<div class="paper-figures-scroll">
<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2606.13387_figures/2606.13387_page2.jpg" alt="Figure 1">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 1.</b> Low-resolution page preview, page 2</figcaption>
</figure>
<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2606.13387_figures/2606.13387_page3.jpg" alt="Figure 2">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 2.</b> Low-resolution page preview, page 3</figcaption>
</figure>
<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2606.13387_figures/2606.13387_page4.jpg" alt="Figure 3">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 3.</b> Low-resolution page preview, page 4</figcaption>
</figure>
<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2606.13387_figures/2606.13387_page5.jpg" alt="Figure 4">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 4.</b> Low-resolution page preview, page 5</figcaption>
</figure>
<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2606.13387_figures/2606.13387_page6.jpg" alt="Figure 5">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 5.</b> Low-resolution page preview, page 6</figcaption>
</figure>
</div>

**Summary.** This paper investigates how mapping fermions to qubits affects the feasibility of running variational quantum simulations for molecular electronic structure. The authors find that certain mappings create artificial 'traps' in the optimization landscape, especially under asymmetric stretching. They propose a novel, adaptive filtering technique that diagnoses these topological failures by monitoring gradient stability, offering a resource-efficient path toward fault-tolerant quantum chemistry.

**Why it may be interesting.** This work directly addresses the practical limitations of applying quantum algorithms to complex chemistry problems, providing a diagnostic tool (the adaptive filter) that moves beyond simple resource counting to diagnose fundamental topological failures in the optimization landscape itself.

<details markdown="1"><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** The study evaluates how representation topologies, specifically arising from fermionic-to-qubit mappings (JW vs. BK), impact the trainability of adaptive quantum chemistry algorithms when simulating multi-reference electronic structures.

**Main result.** Asymmetric molecular distortions cause the Bravyi-Kitaev mapping to induce an optimization trapping effect, while preserving point-group symmetry structurally protects the landscape; a dynamic shot-allocation filter can mitigate these traps.

**Method.** The authors use ADAPT-VQE on stretched molecules and introduce a covariance-driven adaptive shot-allocation filter that monitors gradient precision ($\epsilon$) to diagnose and halt computation upon detecting representation-induced flat-lined states.

**Model / system.** The simulation models molecular electronic structure using the Hamiltonian mapped into an active space, tested on highly stretched configurations of LiH, BeH2, and H2O. The core computational challenge involves mapping fermionic operators to qubits via JW or BK transformations.

**Key observables.** Optimization landscape trainability, energy convergence status (Clean Convergence vs. Gradient Stall), gradient precision ($\epsilon$), and Pauli Term count.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Highly stretched geometries ($2 	imes Re$) of LiH, BeH2, H2O; the adaptive threshold $\epsilon$; and the choice between JW and BK mappings.

**Assumptions / limitations.** The analysis assumes that mapping representation is a critical factor in maintaining landscape trainability, and it proposes an adaptive filter to manage resource allocation based on gradient diagnostics.

**Figures summary.** Table 1 compares performance metrics (Pauli Terms, Energy, Depth, Status) across different systems and mappers. Table 2 lists nuclear coordinates for the benchmark molecules. Appendix A contains telemetry logs showing convergence behavior.

**Paper structure.** The paper systematically analyzes ADAPT-VQE on stretched molecules, comparing JW and BK mappings to identify topological trapping effects. It then introduces a novel adaptive shot-allocation filter that diagnoses these traps by monitoring gradient precision ($\epsilon$) and triggering termination when symmetry constraints cause stagnation.

</details>

<details markdown="1"><summary>Abstract</summary>

Evaluating the trainability of adaptive quantum chemistry algorithms under multi-reference static correlation requires understanding how representation topologies intertwine with molecular geometry. We systematically expose a deep physical dependence on point-group symmetry by evaluating a spin-conserved SUSD operator pool across highly stretched configurations (2 x Re) of asymmetric LiH, symmetric BeH2, and asymmetric H2O. Under asymmetric distortions, the non-local mapping constraints of the Bravyi-Kitaev transformation create an optimization trapping effect--an encodement-locked manifestation of the broader barren plateau crisis. Crucially, by comparing these to the symmetrical stretching baseline of BeH2, we demonstrate that the preservation of point-group symmetry structurally protects the optimization landscape, proving that ansatz symmetry restrictions are necessary but insufficient without accounting for the underlying fermion-to-qubit representation. While current methods rely on numerical pruning to throttle pool sizes, our structural approach establishes that the mapping representation remains a critical factor in maintaining landscape trainability. Furthermore, exploiting structural overlap within our pool, we introduce a covariance-driven, adaptive shot-allocation filter. Diverging from static energy-variance minimization frameworks, our allocation engine operates as a dynamic runtime diagnostic tool. By continuously monitoring the gradient precision threshold epsilon, it aggressively prunes dead symmetry channels and triggers an automated circuit-termination sequence upon detecting representation-induced flat-lined states (dE/dtheta approx 0). This integration of algebraic measurement reuse with topology-aware statistical filtering provides a promising, resource-efficient strategy for executing deep variational algorithms on early fault-tolerant architectures.

</details>

<sub>[↑ back to top](#top)</sub>

<a id="paper-2606.13290"></a>
### [Understanding quantum behaviors of an electron in a uniform magnetic field alternatively](http://arxiv.org/abs/2606.13290v1)

**Authors:** Jin-Ming Wang, Yuan-Zao Gao, Dai-Lin Cun, Jian Jing  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** other · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2606.13290v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks

<div class="figure-strip-hint">↔ Scroll figures horizontally</div>
<div class="paper-figures-scroll">
<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2606.13290_figures/2606.13290_fig1.jpg" alt="Figure 1">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 1.</b> FIG. 1: The factors f1(r), f2(r) and partitioned kinetic angular momentum integrand for Landau eigenstates with m = −1 and varying radial quantum numbers nr (setting magnetic length a = 1). Left panels display the factor f1(r) = mr + 1</figcaption>
</figure>
</div>

**Summary.** This theoretical work analyzes electron motion in a magnetic field, focusing on states with negative angular momentum where the net probability current vanishes. The authors demonstrate this zero current results from an exact cancellation between opposing inner (clockwise) and outer (counterclockwise) circulations across a critical radius. This reveals that the quantum state possesses two competing rotational components whose balance dictates the system's dynamics.

**Why it may be interesting.** It provides a deep, non-trivial dynamical interpretation of degeneracy by mapping it onto a competitive balance between two distinct rotational components, which is valuable for understanding quantum symmetries.

<details markdown="1"><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** The paper investigates the physical interpretation of the vanishing total probability current for electron states with negative angular quantum numbers in a uniform magnetic field.

**Main result.** The zero net current is shown to arise from an exact cancellation between opposing clockwise (inner) and counterclockwise (outer) circulations, revealing an intrinsic bidirectional flow structure.

**Method.** Theoretical analysis involving the decomposition of the probability current density into canonical and gauge parts, and defining a critical radius that partitions the system's flow.

**Model / system.** The model is an electron confined by a uniform magnetic field ($\mathbf{B}$), leading to Landau levels. The analysis uses the eigenstates $\psi_{n_r, m}(r, \varphi)$ derived from the corresponding Hamiltonian.

**Key observables.** Probability current density ($\mathbf{J}$), partitioned kinetic angular momentum ($\langle L_{	ext{kin}}^{	ext{in}} angle$ and $\langle L_{	ext{kin}}^{	ext{out}} angle$), and the critical radius ($r_c$).

**Important parameters / regimes.** Angular quantum number ($m$), radial quantum number ($n_r$), and the magnetic field strength ($\mathbf{B}$).

**Assumptions / limitations.** The analysis relies on the gauge invariance of the probability current density, which is crucial for physical interpretation.

**Figures summary.** Tables illustrate how inner and outer rotational components evolve with $|m|$ and $n_r$, showing synchronous growth/decay while maintaining a constant difference corresponding to $\langle L_{	ext{kin}} angle$.

**Paper structure.** The paper progresses from establishing the vanishing total current for $m<0$ via cancellation, to defining the critical radius $r_c$, and finally analyzing the resulting bidirectional competition structure in terms of kinetic angular momentum.

</details>

<details markdown="1"><summary>Abstract</summary>

Quantum mechanically, an electron moving in a uniform magnetic field forms Landau levels. A curious feature is that for states with a negative angular quantum number, the total probability current vanishes, which appears to contradict the classical picture of cyclotron motion. While a geometric interpretation based on classical orbits exists, alternative interpretations remain of interest. In this paper, we examine the probability current density and identify a critical radius that naturally partitions the plane into an inner clockwise-flow region and an outer counterclockwise-flow region. We show that the vanishing total current results from an exact cancellation between these two regions. Furthermore, by defining a partitioned kinetic angular momentum with respect to the critical radius, we reveal an intrinsic competitive structure: the electron simultaneously carries two opposing rotational components. The negative quantum number manifests in the strength of the inner counter-rotation, while the net kinetic angular momentum remains positive. This bidirectional flow picture also provides a dynamical interpretation of the infinite degeneracy of Landau levels.

</details>

<sub>[↑ back to top](#top)</sub>

</details>

<a id="paper-2606.12933"></a>
### [A micromagnetic model with bidirectional magneto-thermal coupling](http://arxiv.org/abs/2606.12933v1)

**Authors:** Peiru Yi, Zian Xia, Weichao Yu  
**Type:** theory · **Category:** statistical mechanics · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2606.12933v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks
**Topic relevance:** `methods for driven-dissipative` **3/5** · `non-equilibrium dynamics` **3/5** · `spintronics-quantum-optics interface` **3/5** · `Keldysh / 2PI / non-Gaussian methods` **2/5** · `correlated / nonlocal dissipation` **2/5** · `driven-dissipative phase transition` **2/5** · `exotic spin models in light-matter` **1/5** · `non-equilibrium universality` **1/5**

**Summary.** This paper develops a self-consistent model coupling stochastic magnetization dynamics with thermal heat transfer. By treating energy dissipation as a feedback source into the thermal bath, it rigorously proves thermodynamic consistency and predicts measurable temperature changes. This advances spin-caloritronics by providing a robust framework for non-equilibrium magneto-thermal studies.

**Why it may be interesting.** This work provides a detailed microscopic foundation for non-equilibrium thermodynamics in magnetic systems, which is crucial for understanding heat transport phenomena relevant to quantum devices.

<details markdown="1"><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** To overcome the limitations of conventional micromagnetic models that use unidirectional coupling, this work establishes a rigorously self-consistent bidirectional magneto-thermal coupling framework.

**Main result.** The coupled system is shown to strictly obey the first law of thermodynamics and spontaneously recovers correct Boltzmann statistics at equilibrium. The model predicts measurable temperature drops ($\Delta T$) in the thermal bath due to magnetic dynamics.

**Method.** The authors integrate the stochastic Landau-Lifshitz-Gilbert (sLLG) equation with a generalized heat transfer equation, utilizing Ito stochastic calculus for rigorous energy balance analysis.

**Model / system.** The system models coupled spin dynamics and thermal evolution in a magnetic material. The core components are the sLLG equation governing magnetization ($\mathbf{m}$) and a heat diffusion equation governing local temperature ($T$).

**Key observables.** Local temperature field $T(\mathbf{r}, t)$, energy exchange mechanism (dissipation vs. work), density of states $g(E)$, and the steady-state temperature reduction $\Delta T$.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Damping coefficient ($\alpha$), thermal conductivity ($\kappa_{	ext{th}}$), initial temperature ($T_0$), and system volume ($\Delta V$).

**Assumptions / limitations.** The analysis often relies on thermodynamic adiabatic approximations, small angle expansions, and the assumption that local energy balance can be closed into a self-consistent loop.

**Figures summary.** Figures illustrate the bidirectional energy exchange (dissipation feeding heat), the time evolution of bath temperature towards steady state, and histograms confirming recovery of Boltzmann statistics.

**Paper structure.** The paper develops the coupled equations by deriving local power balances, applies Ito calculus to ensure thermodynamic consistency, validates equilibrium recovery via statistical checks, and finally simulates macroscopic energy exchange effects like $\Delta T$.

</details>

<details markdown="1"><summary>Abstract</summary>

Most conventional micromagnetic frameworks in spin caloritronics rely on a unidirectional coupling approximation, wherein thermal fluctuations drive magnetization dynamics while the feedback of magnetic dissipation onto the thermal reservoir is neglected. Here, we establish a rigorously self-consistent bidirectional magneto-thermal coupling model by integrating the stochastic Landau-Lifshitz-Gilbert (sLLG) equation with a generalized heat transfer equation. In this closed-loop framework, the local temperature acts as a dynamical variable, and the damping-induced dissipation alongside stochastic work dynamically feeds back into the thermal bath as localized heat sources. Utilizing Ito stochastic calculus, we analytically prove that this coupled system strictly obeys the first law of thermodynamics and spontaneously recovers the correct Boltzmann statistics at equilibrium. Spatially resolved micromagnetic simulations further validate the energy exchange mechanism, capturing the finite-bath temperature reduction induced by spatial variation of magnetic moments and the modified density of states under exchange interactions. This bidirectional framework provides a robust microscopic foundation for investigating complex nonequilibrium magneto-thermal dynamics, such as the unidirectional spin-wave heat conveyer effect, paving the way for advanced spin-caloritronic applications.

</details>

### [Micron-sized magnonic 3-port rectilinear circulator](http://arxiv.org/abs/2606.13540v1)

**Summary.** This paper reports the experimental realization and characterization of a micron-sized magnon circulator using spin-waves in YIG thin films. By exploiting chiral excitation via nanowire gratings, they demonstrated robust non-reciprocal signal routing between three ports. This work advances integrated magnonics for next-generation microwave devices.

**Why it may be interesting.** While focused on solid-state microwave physics, the concept of engineered wave propagation with inherent directionality and tunable dispersion relations shares mathematical parallels with controlled energy flow in quantum optical cavities or waveguide arrays.

<details markdown="1"><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** The development of miniaturized non-reciprocal microwave technologies compatible with integrated circuit architectures is critical for modern information technology.

**Main result.** The authors successfully demonstrated genuine spin-wave circulation in a micron-sized magnon circulator, confirming the feasibility of such devices for integrated magnonic circuits.

**Method.** Characterization was performed using 3-port spin-wave spectroscopy with a Vector Network Analyzer (VNA), measuring scattering parameters and extracting dynamic inductance spectra.

**Model / system.** The system is a prototype magnon circulator fabricated on a thin Yttrium Iron Garnet (YIG) film, utilizing chiral excitation of spin-waves via nanowire gratings to achieve non-reciprocity.

**Key observables.** Spin-wave circulation ($\Delta S_{ij}$ asymmetry), group velocity ($v_g$), attenuation length ($	ext{L}_{	ext{att}}$), and frequency/field dependence of scattering parameters.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Operating frequencies (2–8 GHz), external magnetic fields ($\pm 100$ mT), grating dimensions, and wavevectors ($k_n$).

**Assumptions / limitations.** The non-reciprocity is governed by the chiral excitation mechanism enabled by the nanowire gratings.

**Figures summary.** Figures show setup schematics, SEM images of prototypes, frequency-field maps confirming circulation asymmetry, and plots detailing field dependence of extracted spin-wave properties like $v_g$ and $	ext{L}_{	ext{att}}$.

**Paper structure.** The paper progresses from identifying the need for miniaturized non-reciprocal devices to presenting the physical mechanism (chiral excitation), followed by detailed experimental characterization across varying fields and frequencies, culminating in analysis of extracted material properties.

</details>

<details markdown="1"><summary>Abstract</summary>

The development of miniaturized non-reciprocal microwave technologies compatible with integrated circuit architectures remains a critical challenge for modern information technology. Here, we present the first experimental characterization of a micron-sized prototypical magnon circulator. Taking advantage of the chiral excitation of spin-waves via nanowire gratings, we propose an original design of a circulator involving three channels of rectilinear and unidirectional spin-wave beams. We demonstrate via a full 3-port spin-wave spectroscopy a genuine spin-wave circulation between the three ports. The narrow frequency band of operation can be tuned over a broad range of frequencies ($2$-$8$ GHz) with both an external field of up to $100$ mT, and the dimensions of the grating specifying the wavevectors. This proposed scheme opens up possibilities for new architectures of integrated and miniaturized non-reciprocal microwave devices.

</details>

### [Real-Time Visualization of the Spatiotemporal Dynamics of 3D Solitons](http://arxiv.org/abs/2606.13456v1)

**Authors:** XinGe Liu, Chaoyang Geng, Yunhan Yu, Lixia Xi, Xiaoguang Zhang, Xiaosheng Xiao  
**Type:** experiment · **Category:** other · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2606.13456v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks
**Topic relevance:** `quantum optics experiment` **3/5** · `analog quantum simulation` **2/5** · `non-equilibrium dynamics` **2/5** · `driven-dissipative phase transition` **1/5** · `entanglement & information structure` **1/5** · `interference shaping light` **1/5** · `non-equilibrium universality` **1/5**

**Summary.** The research presents a novel experimental technique combining spatial sampling (ASTM) and spectral analysis (DFT) to visualize 3D soliton dynamics in multimode fiber lasers. They demonstrate that the formation of these complex solitons involves a distinct stabilization phase characterized by high spatial coherence, which precedes noticeable spectral broadening. This work provides crucial diagnostic tools for advancing ultrafast laser design.

**Why it may be interesting.** This work is highly relevant to quantum optics and open quantum systems because it pushes the boundaries of characterizing complex nonlinear wave phenomena in high-dimensional optical media, which shares mathematical parallels with many-body physics problems.

<details markdown="1"><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** The primary challenge addressed is achieving real-time visualization of the complex spatiotemporal dynamics of three-dimensional (3D) optical solitons.

**Main result.** The study reveals that during 3D soliton birth, the beam profile stabilizes and exhibits high spatial coherence *before* significant spectral broadening occurs, providing critical insights into multimode laser design.

**Method.** The authors developed and utilized Array-based Spatial Sampling with Time-Division Multiplexing (ASTM) combined with Time-Stretch Dispersive Fourier Transformation (DFT) for simultaneous measurement.

**Model / system.** The experiment uses a multimode fiber laser system operating in the regime of Spatiotemporal Mode-Locking (STML), which supports 3D solitons exhibiting rich nonlinear dynamics beyond simple 1D soliton behavior.

**Key observables.** Spatiotemporal beam profile evolution, total soliton energy evolution, cross-correlation coefficient between adjacent roundtrip beam profiles, and pulse-resolved spectral/beam evolutions.

**Important parameters / regimes.** The system operates with a fundamental repetition frequency of $\sim 55.5 	ext{ MHz}$ (roundtrip time $\sim 18 	ext{ ns}$) and involves multimode fibers supporting up to $\sim 100$ LP modes.

**Assumptions / limitations.** ASTM measurements provide an integrated beam profile rather than the full spatiotemporal distribution, which is a noted limitation.

**Figures summary.** Figures illustrate the ASTM setup schematic, typical transient behavior showing energy and cross-correlation changes, and detailed comparisons of soliton formation processes using both DFT spectral data and ASTM beam measurements over many roundtrips.

**Paper structure.** The paper introduces the challenge of 3D soliton visualization, details the novel ASTM/DFT measurement technique, presents observations on soliton birth dynamics (stability preceding spectral broadening), and concludes with implications for ultrafast laser design.

</details>

<details markdown="1"><summary>Abstract</summary>

Three-dimensional (3D) optical solitons bear far stronger relevance to multi-dimensional nonlinear dynamics prevalent in complex physical, chemical and biological systems than conventional 1D solitons, and they support far richer and more intricate phenomena arising from their spatiotemporal degrees of freedom. However, real-time recording of 3D soliton evolution with simultaneous spatiotemporal resolution remains a critical challenging. Here, we demonstrate long-term real-time visualization of 3D soliton dynamics with spatiotemporal resolution using high-speed photodetectors combined with joint space- and time-division multiplexing. We visually capture complex transient behaviors of 3D solitons in a multimode fiber laser and, by integrating our method with the time-stretch technique, simultaneously record pulse-resolved beam and spectral evolutions. We observe that during the birth of 3D solitons, the highly multimode beam stabilizes for a substantial interval prior to spectral broadening, indicating that a large number of transverse modes have already locked before longitudinal mode proliferation. These findings highlight the critical importance of real-time spatiotemporal visualization for advancing ultrafast multimode laser design and delivering new insights into high-dimensional nonlinear dynamics.

</details>

<a id="paper-2606.13609"></a>
### [Temporal glide symmetry enforces a parity sideband selection rule in scalar bulk media](http://arxiv.org/abs/2606.13609v1)

**Authors:** Miguel Camacho  
**Type:** both · **Category:** other · **PDF:** <https://arxiv.org/pdf/2606.13609v1>  
**Analysis basis:** full PDF text, analyzed in chunks
**Topic relevance:** `methods for driven-dissipative` **3/5** · `non-equilibrium dynamics` **3/5** · `analog quantum simulation` **1/5** · `correlated / nonlocal dissipation` **1/5** · `driven-dissipative phase transition` **1/5** · `interference shaping light` **1/5** · `non-equilibrium universality` **1/5**

<div class="figure-strip-hint">↔ Scroll figures horizontally</div>
<div class="paper-figures-scroll">
<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2606.13609_figures/2606.13609_fig1.jpg" alt="Figure 1">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 1.</b> Figure 1: Symmetry structure of synchronous versus time-glide modulation of a trilayer waveguide.</figcaption>
</figure>
<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2606.13609_figures/2606.13609_fig2.jpg" alt="Figure 2">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 2.</b> Figure 2: Static-parity hybridization from time-glide modulation and its phase and period controls. a,</figcaption>
</figure>
<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2606.13609_figures/2606.13609_fig3.jpg" alt="Figure 3">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 3.</b> Figure 3: Spectrally isolated parity conversion in a time-glide-modulated waveguide section. a, FDTD</figcaption>
</figure>
<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2606.13609_figures/2606.13609_fig4.jpg" alt="Figure 4">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 4.</b> Figure 4: Exact parity–sideband selection rule in finite-section scattering. a, Wrong-parity fraction</figcaption>
</figure>
</div>

**Summary.** The paper demonstrates that temporal glide symmetry imposes an exact parity selection rule governing how electromagnetic energy converts between sidebands in time-modulated waveguides. By comparing this 'glide' drive to a standard 'synchronous' drive, the authors prove that only specific, alternating transverse parities are allowed for emission at different frequency harmonics. This offers a new design principle for controlling light coupling in optical devices.

**Why it may be interesting.** This work provides a powerful example of how underlying discrete symmetries (like glide symmetry) can impose non-trivial, measurable selection rules on energy transport in engineered photonic systems, which is highly relevant for designing frequency converters or quantum light sources.

<details markdown="1"><summary>Detailed structure</summary>

**Main problem.** The study investigates how temporal glide symmetry imposes a strict, quantifiable selection rule on energy conversion between different frequency sidebands in time-modulated photonic waveguides.

**Main result.** Temporal glide enforces an exact parity selection rule: the transverse parity of any Floquet eigenstate must alternate with its sideband index ($m$), which is confirmed by showing forbidden output channels are suppressed to numerical zero.

**Method.** The work combines theoretical analysis using Floquet theory (operator algebra, eigenvector projection) with numerical validation via finite-section time-domain simulations (FDTD).

**Model / system.** The system modeled is a scalar trilayer waveguide whose permittivity is modulated periodically in time. The comparison is drawn between 'synchronous' and 'time-glide' modulation protocols.

**Key observables.** Parity content of Floquet eigenstates, the violation metric ($V$), wrong-parity fraction per sideband ($W_m$), and spectral reorganization patterns.

**Important parameters / regimes.** Modulation phase delay ($\phi$), sideband index ($m$), contrast in permittivity modulation ($\Delta\epsilon_r$), and time period ($T$).

**Assumptions / limitations.** The analysis is restricted to scalar relative-permittivity modulation, meaning parity mixing must originate solely from the temporal glide drive itself.

**Figures summary.** Figures compare spectral evolution under synchronous vs. time-glide drives, showing reorganization of coupling sectors in the latter case; other figures quantify the vanishingly small power leakage into symmetry-forbidden channels at the glide point.

**Paper structure.** The paper progresses from establishing the physical models and symmetries (synchronous vs. time-glide) to deriving the selection rule theoretically using Floquet operators, and finally verifying this rule rigorously through quantitative metrics ($V$, $W_m$) in both theoretical matching and FDTD simulations.

</details>

<details markdown="1"><summary>Abstract</summary>

Symmetry is a powerful way to control coupling between photonic mode families. In spatially periodic structures, glide symmetry can protect band contacts and suppress stop bands. Here we show a different role for temporal glide, a spatiotemporal counterpart combining reflection with a half-period time translation. In a scalar time-modulated trilayer waveguide, temporal glide imposes an exact selection rule linking frequency conversion to transverse-mode symmetry: the parity content of every Floquet eigenstate alternates with sideband index, up to a state-dependent sign. In scattering, this means that a mode of definite parity can emit only into the opposite transverse parity at odd sidebands and into the same parity at even sidebands. We verify the rule directly in bulk Floquet eigenstates and in finite-section time-domain simulations. An incident odd waveguide mode is converted into an even frequency sideband, while all symmetry-forbidden output channels at the analysed sidebands are suppressed to numerically negligible values. Rather than acting as a temporal copy of spatial-glide band sticking, temporal glide provides a distinct symmetry principle for converting electromagnetic energy between selected modes and frequencies.

</details>

<sub>[↑ back to top](#top)</sub>

### [Revealing nonvolatile behaviors in magneto-thermal switching using microstructure-controlled superconducting composites](http://arxiv.org/abs/2606.12778v1)

<img src="2606.12778_figures/2606.12778_fig3.jpg" alt="Figure 3">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 3.</b> FIG 3. Magnetic field H dependence of the thermal conductivity κ at 2.5, 4.0, and 10.0 K for the Sn/Pb multilayered composites with the repetition number n of (a) 1, (b) 4, (c) 7, (d) 10, and (e) 13. The closed circles indicate the data obtained with increasing H, whereas the open circles with decreasing H. Arrows in (c) also indicates the sweeping direction of H.</figcaption>
</figure>
<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2606.12778_figures/2606.12778_fig4.jpg" alt="Figure 4">
<figcaption class="paper-figure-caption"><b>Fig 4.</b> FIG 4. The repetition number n dependence of nonvolatile MTSR for the Sn/Pb multilayered composites at 2.5, 4.0 and 10.0 K.</figcaption>
</figure>
<figure class="paper-figure-card">
<img src="2606.12778_figures/2606.12778_fig5.jpg" alt="Figure 5">
